<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Shirley Manson</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Shirley Ann Manson</b> (born 26 August 1966) is a Scottish singer, songwriter, musician and actress. She is the lead singer of the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)" title="Garbage (band)">Garbage</a>. For much of her international career Manson commuted between her home city of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> and the United States to record with Garbage; she now lives and works in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changingface_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-changingface-1">[1]</a></sup> Manson gained media attention for her forthright style, rebellious attitude, and distinctive voice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkling_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-darkling-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronicle_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph1_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vagazine_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-vagazine-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson's musical career began in her teens when she was approached to perform backing vocals and keyboards for Scottish band <a href="/wiki/Goodbye_Mr._Mackenzie" title="Goodbye Mr. Mackenzie">Goodbye Mr Mackenzie</a>. Quickly she developed into a prominent member of the group and developed a formidable stage presence. Manson was approached by her band's record label with the idea of launching her as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solo_artist" title="Solo artist">solo artist</a>, and recorded an album with her band under the <a href="/wiki/Angelfish_(band)" title="Angelfish (band)">Angelfish</a> name. After seeing Manson in an Angelfish <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">video</a> broadcast only once on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/120_Minutes" title="120 Minutes">120 Minutes</a></i>, Garbage invited Manson to audition and record vocals on a couple of unfinished songs; she eventually co-wrote and co-produced an entire album with the band. The resulting self-titled debut, <i><a href="/wiki/Garbage_(album)" title="Garbage (album)">Garbage</a></i>, was a critically acclaimed, worldwide hit, and was followed by four studio albums, including the multiple <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>-nominated <i><a href="/wiki/Version_2.0" title="Version 2.0">Version 2.0</a></i>, and a <a href="/wiki/Absolute_Garbage" title="Absolute Garbage">greatest hits album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup> Garbage toured worldwide and sold 12 million records over ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Manson began to write and record solo material after Garbage was put on "hiatus" and in 2008 was cast in her first professional acting role on the second, final season of <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator:_The_Sarah_Connor_Chronicles" title="Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles">Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles</a></i> as series regular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_Weaver" title="Catherine Weaver">Catherine Weaver</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Shapeshifting#In_popular_culture" title="Shapeshifting">liquid metal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-1001" title="T-1001">T-1001</a> <a href="/wiki/Terminator_(character_concept)" title="Terminator (character concept)">Terminator</a>. Manson returned to the recording studio in 2010 to write and produce material for the group's fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Not_Your_Kind_of_People" title="Not Your Kind of People">Not Your Kind of People</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-album5_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-album5-7">[7]</a></sup> who have since followed up with a sixth album <i><a href="/wiki/Strange_Little_Birds" title="Strange Little Birds">Strange Little Birds</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_career">Early life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="2362" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg/220px-Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg/330px-Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg/440px-Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Overview01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Manson was born and raised in the city of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> in central Scotland.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Shirley Ann Manson was born to John Mitchell and Muriel Flora Manson (née MacKay) in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup> John Mitchell, a descendant from the fishing community of <a href="/wiki/Northmavine" title="Northmavine">Northmavine</a>, Shetland, was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_lecturer" title="University lecturer">university lecturer</a> while Muriel was a <a href="/wiki/Big_band" title="Big band">big band</a> singer, who had been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adopted" title="Adopted">adopted</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Lothian" title="Lothian">Lothian</a>-based family at an early age (and took on the family name MacDonald).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup> Shirley was named after an aunt who was herself named after <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Bront%C3%AB" title="Charlotte Brontë">Charlotte Brontë</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Shirley_(novel)" title="Shirley (novel)">Shirley</a>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheFace98_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheFace98-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-notofu_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-notofu-9">[9]</a></sup> She was born with two years between both older sister Lindy-Jayne and younger sister Sarah,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edinburgh_ambassador_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edinburgh_ambassador-10">[10]</a></sup> and was brought up in the <a href="/wiki/Comely_Bank" title="Comely Bank">Comely Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stockbridge,_Edinburgh" title="Stockbridge, Edinburgh">Stockbridge</a> areas of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Family_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Family-11">[11]</a></sup> She attended <a href="/wiki/Broughton_High_School,_Edinburgh" title="Broughton High School, Edinburgh">Broughton High School, Edinburgh</a>. Manson's childhood education was informed by the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> (her father was also her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunday_School" title="Sunday School">Sunday School</a> teacher), until the age of 12, when she rebelled against organized religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS1998_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS1998-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson's first public performance was in 1970, at age four, with her older sister, in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_amateur_theatre" title="Edinburgh amateur theatre">an amateur show</a> held at the local <a href="/wiki/Church_Hill,_Edinburgh" title="Church Hill, Edinburgh">Church Hill Theatre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup> Enrolled at Flora Stevenson Primary School, Manson received instruction in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recorder_(instrument)" title="Recorder (instrument)">recorder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarinet" title="Clarinet">clarinet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiddle" title="Fiddle">fiddle</a>, and learned ballet and piano from <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Extramural&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Extramural (page does not exist)">extramural</a> classes at age seven. Manson was a member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Girlguiding_UK" title="Girlguiding UK">Girlguiding UK</a> throughout this period of her youth as a <a href="/wiki/Brownie_(Girl_Guides)" title="Brownie (Girl Guides)">Brownie</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Girl_Guiding_and_Girl_Scouting" title="Girl Guiding and Girl Scouting">Guide</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Manson attended the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Edinburgh_Music_School" title="City of Edinburgh Music School">City of Edinburgh Music School</a>, the music department of <a href="/wiki/Broughton_High_School,_Edinburgh" title="Broughton High School, Edinburgh">Broughton High</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edinburgh_ambassador_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Edinburgh_ambassador-10">[10]</a></sup> While at Broughton, Manson became an active member of its drama group, performing in amateur dramatic and musical performances such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_American_Dream_(play)" title="The American Dream (play)">The American Dream</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz" title="The Wonderful Wizard of Oz">The Wizard of Oz</a></i>, while also singing with the Waverley Singers, a local girl <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choir</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup> Other notable members of the drama group included Hilary MacLean, Neil Bett, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rebecca_Pigeon" title="Rebecca Pigeon">Rebecca Pigeon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sara_Stewart" title="Sara Stewart">Sara Stewart</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> while a production of <i>Maurice the Minotaur</i> (in which Manson played a prophet) during the 1981 <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Festival_Fringe" title="Edinburgh Festival Fringe">Edinburgh Festival Fringe</a> was awarded a Fringe First award by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scotsman" title="The Scotsman">The Scotsman</a></i> newspaper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>While she enjoyed primary school, Manson was <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullied</a> while in her first year at secondary school, causing her to suffer from depression, <a href="/wiki/Body_dysmorphic_disorder" title="Body dysmorphic disorder">body dysmorphic disorder</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changing_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-changing-15">[15]</a></sup> and engage in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-injury" title="Self-injury">self-injury</a>: she carried a sharp object in the laces of her boots and cut herself when she felt low self-esteem, stress or anxiety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The bullying stopped when Manson associated herself with a rebel crowd – which resulted in her rebelling herself; playing <a href="/wiki/Truancy" title="Truancy">truant</a> for most of her final year at school,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Family_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Family-11">[11]</a></sup> smoking <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sniffing_glue" title="Sniffing glue">sniffing glue</a>, drinking, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shoplift" title="Shoplift">shoplifting</a>, and on one occasion breaking into <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Zoo" title="Edinburgh Zoo">Edinburgh Zoo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FHM_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FHM-17">[17]</a></sup> Manson's first job was volunteer work in a local hospital's cafeteria, then as a breakfast waitress at a local hotel before spending five years as a shop assistant for <a href="/wiki/Miss_Selfridge" title="Miss Selfridge">Miss Selfridge</a>, beginning on the make-up counter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FHM_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-FHM-17">[17]</a></sup> Manson was eventually moved into stockrooms because of her attitude toward customers. Manson became well known throughout Edinburgh's <a href="/wiki/Nightclub" title="Nightclub">clubbing scene</a>, and making use of free samples from Miss Selfridge, styled hair for a number of local bands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RecordCollector_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-RecordCollector-18">[18]</a></sup> Manson also briefly <a href="/wiki/Model_(person)" title="Model (person)">modelled</a> clothing for <i><a href="/wiki/Jackie_(magazine)" title="Jackie (magazine)">Jackie</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goodbye_Mr_Mackenzie">Goodbye Mr Mackenzie</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Goodbye Mr Mackenzie">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Goodbye_Mr._Mackenzie" title="Goodbye Mr. Mackenzie">Goodbye Mr. Mackenzie</a></div>
<p>Manson's first musical experiences came from briefly singing with local Edinburgh acts The Wild Indians and performed backing vocals with Autumn 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RecordCollector_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-RecordCollector-18">[18]</a></sup> While she was acting in her group, Manson was approached by <a href="/wiki/Goodbye_Mr._Mackenzie" title="Goodbye Mr. Mackenzie">Goodbye Mr. Mackenzie</a>'s lead Martin Metcalfe to join his band. Manson embarked on a relationship with Metcalfe initially, but remained involved after splitting from him and became a prominent member of the group, performing keyboards, backing vocals and becoming involved in the band's business side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Manson's first release with the Mackenzies was a <a href="/wiki/Youth_Training_Scheme" title="Youth Training Scheme">YTS</a> release of "Death of a Salesman" in 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RecordCollector_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-RecordCollector-18">[18]</a></sup> The group signed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_label" title="Major label">major label</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Record_deal" title="Record deal">record deal</a> with <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a> in 1987, and they released their first album <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Deeds_and_Dirty_Rags" title="Good Deeds and Dirty Rags">Good Deeds and Dirty Rags</a></i>, and their only <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Top 40</a> hit "The Rattler". In 1990, the group's contract was transferred to <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a>, another <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> label, but after two singles failed to chart Parlophone declined to release the group's second album <i><a href="/wiki/Hammer_and_Tongs" title="Hammer and Tongs">Hammer and Tongs</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mackenzie_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-mackenzie-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gary_Kurfirst" title="Gary Kurfirst">Gary Kurfirst</a>, who managed <a href="/wiki/Talking_Heads" title="Talking Heads">Talking Heads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Harry" title="Debbie Harry">Deborah Harry</a>, bought the Mackenzies contract and issued their second album through his own label <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_Records" title="Radioactive Records">Radioactive</a>, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/MCA_Records" title="MCA Records">MCA</a>. After another single failed to chart, the group were persuaded to leave Radioactive by their management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mackenzie_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-mackenzie-21">[21]</a></sup> The Mackenzies continued to write material; Manson was also given the opportunity to record lead vocals on a number of tracks planned for the band's third album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-angelfishbirth_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-angelfishbirth-22">[22]</a></sup> Although MCA had no desire to further their commitments to Goodbye Mr. Mackenzie, the label expressed interest in recording an album with Manson, and after hearing several <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demos</a>, Kurfirst signed Manson to Radioactive as a solo artist, with the remaining Mackenzies performing as her backing band to circumvent the band's existing deal with MCA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-8"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mackenzie_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-mackenzie-21">[21]</a></sup> Manson's contract obligated her to deliver at least one album and, at the sole option of Radioactive, up to six additional albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radioactive_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Radioactive-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angelfish">Angelfish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Angelfish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Angelfish_(band)" title="Angelfish (band)">Angelfish (band)</a></div>
<p>Recording under the name <a href="/wiki/Angelfish_(band)" title="Angelfish (band)">Angelfish</a>, and using some of the newly written material and a previously released Mackenzie <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B-side" title="B-side">b-side</a>, Manson and the group recorded the tracks that would make up the <i><a href="/wiki/Angelfish_(album)" title="Angelfish (album)">Angelfish</a></i> album in <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a> with <a href="/wiki/Talking_Heads" title="Talking Heads">Talking Heads</a>' <a href="/wiki/Chris_Frantz" title="Chris Frantz">Chris Frantz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tina_Weymouth" title="Tina Weymouth">Tina Weymouth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMExhibition_6-9"><a href="#cite_note-SMExhibition-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mackenzie_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-mackenzie-21">[21]</a></sup> A lead in track "<a href="/wiki/Suffocate_Me" title="Suffocate Me">Suffocate Me</a>" was sent to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_radio" title="College radio">college radio</a> where it was well received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RecordCollector_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-RecordCollector-18">[18]</a></sup> <i>Angelfish</i> and second single "<a href="/wiki/Heartbreak_To_Hate" title="Heartbreak To Hate">Heartbreak To Hate</a>" followed in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RecordCollector_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-RecordCollector-18">[18]</a></sup> Angelfish toured the United States, Canada, France, Belgium, and co-supported <a href="/wiki/Live_(band)" title="Live (band)">Live</a> on a tour of North America, along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vic_Chestnutt" title="Vic Chestnutt">Vic Chestnutt</a>. The music video for "Suffocate Me" was aired on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/120_Minutes" title="120 Minutes">120 Minutes</a></i>. Producer and musician <a href="/wiki/Steve_Marker" title="Steve Marker">Steve Marker</a> caught the broadcast and thought Manson would be a great singer for his band, Garbage, which also featured producers <a href="/wiki/Duke_Erikson" title="Duke Erikson">Duke Erikson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Butch_Vig" title="Butch Vig">Butch Vig</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Garbage">Garbage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Garbage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)" title="Garbage (band)">Garbage (band)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="900" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG/170px-%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG/255px-%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG/340px-%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A8%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8_%D0%9C%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B5.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shirley Manson performing live with <a href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)" title="Garbage (band)">Garbage</a> during the band's 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/Not_Your_Kind_of_People_World_Tour" title="Not Your Kind of People World Tour">Not Your Kind of People World Tour</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vig invited Manson to Smart Studios to sing on a couple of tracks. After an unsuccessful audition, she returned to Angelfish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-24">[24]</a></sup> Manson admitted she felt intimidated showcasing herself to Vig, who produced bands she admired such as <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sonic_Youth" title="Sonic Youth">Sonic Youth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Smashing_Pumpkins" title="The Smashing Pumpkins">The Smashing Pumpkins</a>, and Vig added that the audition's disorganized nature along with the Americans not understanding Manson's Scottish accent caused communication problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spin_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-spin-25">[25]</a></sup> At the end of the Live tour, Angelfish imploded and Manson returned to Smart for a second try. She began to work on the then-skeletal origins of some songs and the band invited her to become a full-time member and finish the album; she co-wrote and co-produced the entire album with the rest of the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radioactive_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Radioactive-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-24">[24]</a></sup> In August 1994, Radioactive gave their permission for Manson to work with Garbage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radioactive_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Radioactive-23">[23]</a></sup> The band's debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Garbage_(album)" title="Garbage (album)">Garbage</a></i> was released in August 1995, and went on to sell over 4 million copies, buoyed by a run of high charting singles including "<a href="/wiki/Only_Happy_When_It_Rains" title="Only Happy When It Rains">Only Happy When It Rains</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Stupid_Girl_(Garbage_song)" title="Stupid Girl (Garbage song)">Stupid Girl</a>." Manson quickly became the public face of the band over the course of a tour that took the band through to the end of 1996. <a href="/wiki/Echo_%26_the_Bunnymen" title="Echo &amp; the Bunnymen">Echo &amp; the Bunnymen</a> had asked Manson to sing on their 1997 <a href="/wiki/Evergreen_(Echo_%26_the_Bunnymen_album)" title="Evergreen (Echo &amp; the Bunnymen album)">comeback album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Face_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Face-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson became the band's chief songwriter for the follow-up record <i><a href="/wiki/Version_2.0" title="Version 2.0">Version 2.0</a></i> which equalled the success of the band's debut record after its May 1998 release. During the two-year tour in support of the record, Manson modelled for <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Klein" title="Calvin Klein">Calvin Klein</a>. Manson lived in hotels throughout the recording periods of the debut and Version 2.0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Face_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Face-26">[26]</a></sup> The group recorded the <a href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough_(song)" title="The World Is Not Enough (song)">theme song</a> to the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough" title="The World Is Not Enough">The World Is Not Enough</a>,</i> and Manson became the third Scotswoman to sing a Bond theme after <a href="/wiki/Lulu_(singer)" title="Lulu (singer)">Lulu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheena_Easton" title="Sheena Easton">Sheena Easton</a>. In the accompanying video, she portrays an <a href="/wiki/Android_(robot)" title="Android (robot)">android</a> assassin. For the recording of Garbage's third record throughout 2000, Manson became one of the first high-profile artists to write a blog online, while she decided to improve her guitar playing for the band's next tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Their third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Garbage" title="Beautiful Garbage">Beautiful Garbage</a></i>, featured Manson's most forward and personal lyrics to date. The album did not sell as well as its predecessors, but Garbage performed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beautiful_Garbage_Tour" title="Beautiful Garbage Tour">a successful world tour</a> in support of it. During a concert at the <a href="/wiki/Roskilde_Festival" title="Roskilde Festival">Roskilde Festival</a>, Manson's voice gave out. She afterwards discovered a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vocal_fold_cyst" title="Vocal fold cyst">vocal fold cyst</a>, and had to undergo corrective surgery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson's lyrics became more overtly political for Garbage's fourth record, 2005's <i><a href="/wiki/Bleed_Like_Me" title="Bleed Like Me">Bleed Like Me</a>,</i> which after the surprise success of lead-in single "<a href="/wiki/Why_Do_You_Love_Me" title="Why Do You Love Me">Why Do You Love Me</a>", posted some of the band's highest chart positions upon release. Garbage began an extended hiatus in October 2005. During this period, in 2007, Garbage reformed to perform a short set at a benefit show to raise cash to pay for <a href="/wiki/Wally_Ingram" title="Wally Ingram">Wally Ingram</a>'s medical treatment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> shared song ideas via the internet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> recorded new material, and filmed a music video<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMWIHvideo_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMWIHvideo-32">[32]</a></sup> to promote the band's <i><a href="/wiki/Absolute_Garbage" title="Absolute Garbage">Absolute Garbage</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greatest_hits" title="Greatest hits">greatest hits</a> compilation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ButchVigInterview_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-ButchVigInterview-33">[33]</a></sup> Garbage returned to the studio in 2010 to write and record material for a fifth album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-album5_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-album5-7">[7]</a></sup> entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Not_Your_Kind_of_People" title="Not Your Kind of People">Not Your Kind of People</a></i> and subsequently released in May 2012, thus ending the band's seven-year hiatus from recording.</p>
<p>Garbage's <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative</a> musical style fuses various genres including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_rock" title="Electronic rock">electronic rock</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-break_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-break-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Industrial_rock" title="Industrial rock">industrial rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grunge" title="Grunge">grunge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trip_hop" title="Trip hop">trip hop</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shoegaze" title="Shoegaze">shoegaze</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitchfork_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vice_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vice-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_work_and_unreleased_album">Solo work and unreleased album</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Solo work and unreleased album">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I had taken some of my solo music into the record label. They didn't really care for the direction I was moving in and I found it really disheartening. They wanted a pop hit, which I understand in terms of making money. I get that. But what they were going to ask of me was something I wasn't prepared to deliver and I felt kind of trapped. I just stopped writing. I just stopped. It was stifling".</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Shirley Manson<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geffen-noir_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-geffen-noir-37">[37]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Manson confirmed in March 2006 that she had begun work on a solo album, working with musician <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Nile" title="The Blue Nile">Paul Buchanan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-break_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-break-34">[34]</a></sup> producer <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kurstin" title="Greg Kurstin">Greg Kurstin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Noir_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Noir-38">[38]</a></sup> and film composer <a href="/wiki/David_Arnold" title="David Arnold">David Arnold</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BB_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-BB-39">[39]</a></sup> stating that she had "no timetable" for completing the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BB_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-BB-39">[39]</a></sup> In 2007, Manson collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Rivers_Cuomo" title="Rivers Cuomo">Rivers Cuomo</a> of <a href="/wiki/Weezer" title="Weezer">Weezer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Manson presented some of her work to Geffen Records in 2008, who found it "too <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">noir</a>", prompting Manson and Geffen to mutually terminate her contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geffen-noir_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-geffen-noir-37">[37]</a></sup> Manson later elaborated, "[Geffen] wanted me to have international radio hits and "be the <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a> of my generation". I kid you not; I am quoting directly."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Manson continued to write material while <a href="/wiki/Unsigned_artist" title="Unsigned artist">without a record deal</a> and had been in talks with <a href="/wiki/David_Byrne" title="David Byrne">David Byrne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ray_Davies" title="Ray Davies">Ray Davies</a> about a potential collaboration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changingface_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-changingface-1">[1]</a></sup> In 2009, Manson posted three <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demos</a> on her Facebook profile, written by her and Kurstin, titled "In the Snow",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Noir_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Noir-38">[38]</a></sup> "Pretty Horses"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and "Lighten Up".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> "Pretty Horses" was later featured in the pilot episode of the show <a href="/wiki/Conviction_(2016_TV_series)" title="Conviction (2016 TV series)">Conviction</a>.</p>
<p>In 2009, Manson announced she was stepping away from music, claiming she got sick of the music industry's new practices and had found more excitement in acting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Manson said she thought about abandoning the music business as soon as 2008, when her mother developed <a href="/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">dementia</a>, and later died, saying that "I didn't want to make music, didn't feel creative. I could barely function." Later that year she reconsidered her words and went back into performing after being asked by friends to sing <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>'s "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars%3F" title="Life on Mars?">Life on Mars?</a>" at their son's memorial. According to Manson, "we were all in so much pain, but it meant so much to them that I could sing that song and so much to me that I was able to do something. It made me realise how much music sustains people. I don't know why I'd turned my back on it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson also worked with a number of artists outside of her solo project, reciting a verse of a <a href="/wiki/Long_poem" title="Long poem">long poem</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Chris_Connelly_(musician)" title="Chris Connelly (musician)">Chris Connelly</a> album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-connelly_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-connelly-46">[46]</a></sup> co-writing and recording a duet with <a href="/wiki/Eric_Avery" title="Eric Avery">Eric Avery</a> for his solo debut<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avery_album_PR_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Avery_album_PR-47">[47]</a></sup> recording with Debbie Harry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and performing backing vocals on a <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Rossdale" title="Gavin Rossdale">Gavin Rossdale</a> track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-DM-49">[49]</a></sup> Although not recording material with them, Manson also performed on-stage with <a href="/wiki/The_Pretenders" title="The Pretenders">The Pretenders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iggy_Pop" title="Iggy Pop">Iggy Pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Incubus_(band)" title="Incubus (band)">Incubus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kings_of_Leon" title="Kings of Leon">Kings of Leon</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_City" title="Atlantic City">Atlantic City</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and twice with <a href="/wiki/No_Doubt" title="No Doubt">No Doubt</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Universal_City,_California" title="Universal City, California">Universal City</a>. Manson also performed in an uncredited role as a <a href="/wiki/Dominatrix" title="Dominatrix">dominatrix</a> in the music video for <a href="/wiki/She_Wants_Revenge" title="She Wants Revenge">She Wants Revenge</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/These_Things" title="These Things">These Things</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Most recently Manson performed vocals on a track written by <a href="/wiki/Serj_Tankian" title="Serj Tankian">Serj Tankian</a> entitled "The Hunger", a single from the rock musical <i>Prometheus Bound</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012, Manson confirmed that work on her solo album had been cancelled, stating the album "[is] dead and buried. We had the funeral. It was sad and I cried a lot but it made such a beautiful corpse that we had an open casket."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Artistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice">Voice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Voice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:300px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"We wanted to work with a female vocalist who didn't have a high, chirpy, quality to her voice, we had discussed who we really respect, and names like Patti Smith and Chrissie Hynde came up. And Shirley had some of the same depth."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Steve_Marker" title="Steve Marker">Steve Marker</a> discussing Manson's voice in an interview with the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_Times_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times-56">[56]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Manson possesses a <a href="/wiki/Contralto" title="Contralto">contralto</a> vocal range,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> which has been noted for its distinctive qualities as well as her emotive delivery. Elysa Gardner of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> stated "one of Garbage's most compelling features is a force of nature: Manson's vocals, which can convey a multitude of emotions without ever coming across as melodramatic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph1_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_Times_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:300px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"We wanted someone who could sing in an understated way, at the moment, a lot of these alterna-rock singers have a tendency to scream. Shirley is just the opposite. By using understatement, she can sound even more subversive."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Butch_Vig" title="Butch Vig">Butch Vig</a> describing Manson's voice in the <i>Los Angeles Times</i> interview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_Times_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times-56">[56]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Reviewing a live <a href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)" title="Garbage (band)">Garbage</a> performance Jon Parales of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> commented, "Temptress, lover, sufferer, scrapper – those have been Ms. Manson's personae since Garbage started in 1995. In other eras she might have been a pop <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torch_singer" title="Torch singer">torch singer</a>, a soul belter or a new-wave frontwoman: a <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Bassey" title="Shirley Bassey">Shirley Bassey</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Dusty_Springfield" title="Dusty Springfield">Dusty Springfield</a>, or a <a href="/wiki/Chrissie_Hynde" title="Chrissie Hynde">Chrissie Hynde</a>. There's a little of each of them in her voice" also stating "In the course of each song she let her voice rise in anger, contempt or passion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Jen Crothers of <i><a href="/wiki/Green_Left_Weekly" title="Green Left Weekly">Green Left Weekly</a></i>, in a review of <i><a href="/wiki/Garbage_(album)" title="Garbage (album)">Garbage</a></i>, remarked that "Manson, vocalist and guitarist, has a powerful voice, which soars and dips like a bird. It can plead or demand. It can sound dreamy or psychotic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Reviewing a 2012 live <a href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)" title="Garbage (band)">Garbage</a> performance, Catherine Gee of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i> noted that Manson "remains a striking performer whose distinctive contralto snarl can still raise the hairs on the back of your neck."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In a review of <i><a href="/wiki/Garbage_(album)" title="Garbage (album)">Garbage</a></i> Stephen Thomas Erlewine of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a></i> described Manson's voice as "thin and airy",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> whilst Mike Diver of the <i><a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a></i> stated Manson owned "a snarl in her voice but [was] equally capable of a purr to melt away any resistance." also adding "even at her most vulnerable, Manson maintains her controlling condition".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences_and_impact">Influences and impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Influences and impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Manson's earliest musical memories were of her mother, who sang with a big band when Manson was a child. Manson was exposed to classic jazz records as she grew up and work by <a href="/wiki/Nina_Simone" title="Nina Simone">Nina Simone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Lee" title="Peggy Lee">Peggy Lee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ella_Fitzgerald" title="Ella Fitzgerald">Ella Fitzgerald</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rebeljukebox_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rebeljukebox-64">[64]</a></sup> Early in Manson's teenage years, she became a fan of <a href="/wiki/Siouxsie_and_the_Banshees" title="Siouxsie and the Banshees">Siouxsie and the Banshees</a> albums <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scream_(album)" title="The Scream (album)">The Scream</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaleidoscope_(Siouxsie_%26_the_Banshees_album)" title="Kaleidoscope (Siouxsie &amp; the Banshees album)">Kaleidoscope</a></i>, and taught herself how to sing listening to those albums, later stating "many of the songs of those two albums were massive loves of my life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Vocalist <a href="/wiki/Siouxsie_Sioux" title="Siouxsie Sioux">Siouxsie Sioux</a> embodied how Manson aspired to be as a teen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rebeljukebox_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rebeljukebox-64">[64]</a></sup> Manson would later write the <a href="/wiki/Foreword" title="Foreword">foreword</a> to <i>Siouxsie &amp; The Banshees: The Authorised Biography</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>At nineteen, Manson discovered <a href="/wiki/Patti_Smith" title="Patti Smith">Patti Smith</a>, and specifically Smith's <i><a href="/wiki/Horses_(album)" title="Horses (album)">Horses</a></i> album, which made a "strong impact" on her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Manson was inspired to learn guitar by <a href="/wiki/Chrissie_Hynde" title="Chrissie Hynde">Chrissie Hynde</a>, who is an admirer of Manson,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> while also appreciating the style of <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Harry" title="Debbie Harry">Debbie Harry</a> of <a href="/wiki/Blondie_(band)" title="Blondie (band)">Blondie</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rebeljukebox_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rebeljukebox-64">[64]</a></sup> whose 2006 <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> induction speech was delivered by Manson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The majority of Manson's influences were female musicians; however she also notes <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> as an inspiring male musician.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rebeljukebox_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rebeljukebox-64">[64]</a></sup> Manson also grew up listening to <a href="/wiki/Nick_Cave" title="Nick Cave">Nick Cave</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheFace98_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-TheFace98-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Clash" title="The Clash">The Clash</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Sugarcubes" title="The Sugarcubes">The Sugarcubes</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theskinny.co.uk_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-theskinny.co.uk-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cocteau_Twins" title="Cocteau Twins">Cocteau Twins</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theskinny.co.uk_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-theskinny.co.uk-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iggy_and_the_Stooges" title="Iggy and the Stooges">Iggy and the Stooges</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Velvet_Underground" title="The Velvet Underground">The Velvet Underground</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Family_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Family-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson's lyrics deal with darker themes, often in a mocking manner. She credits that to her Scottish psyche that leads to preferring depressing themes, and the fact she always felt like an outsider, even within Garbage – "I’m the odd one out by default. I’m the only girl, I’m younger than they are, they’ve all known each other for 40 years, or something crazy like that. So I always felt, like, off the centre of things."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spin_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-spin-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson has been credited with inspiring a new generation of female artists; including Ritzy Bryan (the lead singer and guitarist of <a href="/wiki/The_Joy_Formidable" title="The Joy Formidable">The Joy Formidable</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Momsen" title="Taylor Momsen">Taylor Momsen</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marina_and_the_Diamonds" title="Marina and the Diamonds">Marina Diamandis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amy_Lee" title="Amy Lee">Amy Lee</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peaches_(musician)" title="Peaches (musician)">Peaches</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Florence_Welch" title="Florence Welch">Florence Welch</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Liz Anjos of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remix_Artist_Collective" title="Remix Artist Collective">RAC</a> and <i>The Pragmatic</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Dee Dee Penny of <a href="/wiki/Dum_Dum_Girls" title="Dum Dum Girls">Dum Dum Girls</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Skylar_Grey" title="Skylar Grey">Skylar Grey</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> as well as her contemporaries such as <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Courtney_Love" title="Courtney Love">Courtney Love</a>. Manson has also personally given her support to <a href="/wiki/Peaches_(musician)" title="Peaches (musician)">Peaches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brody_Dalle" title="Brody Dalle">Brody Dalle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karen_O" title="Karen O">Karen O</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skylar_Grey" title="Skylar Grey">Skylar Grey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lana_Del_Rey" title="Lana Del Rey">Lana Del Rey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Screaming_Females" title="Screaming Females">Screaming Females</a> and <a href="/wiki/Le_Butcherettes" title="Le Butcherettes">Le Butcherettes</a> at the beginning of their respective careers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Manson_discography" title="Shirley Manson discography">Shirley Manson discography</a></div>

<p>The first time Manson contributed her vocals to a project separately from any of her bands was in 1998, when she performed vocals for the chorus of a Garbage-produced <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remix</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fun_Lovin%27_Criminals" title="Fun Lovin' Criminals">Fun Lovin' Criminals</a> 1999 single "<a href="/wiki/Korean_Bodega" title="Korean Bodega">Korean Bodega</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flckbremix_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-flckbremix-88">[88]</a></sup> Due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Litigation" title="Litigation">litigation</a> problems surrounding Manson's contractual obligation to Radioactive Records, further collaborations with both Fun Lovin' Criminals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Moby" title="Moby">Moby</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> were unable to proceed.</p>
<p>Manson teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Manson" title="Marilyn Manson">Marilyn Manson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Sk%C3%B6ld" title="Tim Sköld">Tim Sköld</a> in 2004 to record a <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover version</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Human_League" title="The Human League">the Human League</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_You_Want_Me" title="Don't You Want Me">Don't You Want Me</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> but both felt the track inappropriate for either acts upcoming albums, and remains unreleased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geffen-noir_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-geffen-noir-37">[37]</a></sup> Later that year, Manson and <a href="/wiki/Brody_Dalle" title="Brody Dalle">Brody Dalle</a> contributed backing vocals to a <a href="/wiki/Queens_of_the_Stone_Age" title="Queens of the Stone Age">Queens of the Stone Age</a> track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In 2006, Manson planned to record a <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a> <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover version</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Instant_Karma:_The_Amnesty_International_Campaign_to_Save_Darfur" title="Instant Karma: The Amnesty International Campaign to Save Darfur">Instant Karma</a></i> charity compilation with bassist <a href="/wiki/Eric_Avery" title="Eric Avery">Eric Avery</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> however a scheduling misunderstanding left them short of time and unable to record the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Manson and Avery eventually co-wrote and recorded "Maybe", a ballad <a href="/wiki/Duet" title="Duet">duet</a> for Avery's album <i><a href="/wiki/Help_Wanted_(Eric_Avery_album)" title="Help Wanted (Eric Avery album)">Help Wanted</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following year, Manson performed backing vocals on a track for <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Rossdale" title="Gavin Rossdale">Gavin Rossdale</a>'s solo album <i><a href="/wiki/Wanderlust" title="Wanderlust">Wanderlust</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DM_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-DM-49">[49]</a></sup> worked with long-time friend Chris Connelly, orating part of a <a href="/wiki/Long_poem" title="Long poem">long poem</a> on his eighth album <i>Forgiveness and Exile</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> and worked on a duet with longtime inspiration Debbie Harry<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> which remains uncompleted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In 2008, Manson contributed to a <a href="/wiki/Dusty_Springfield" title="Dusty Springfield">Dusty Springfield</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribute_album" title="Tribute album">tribute album</a>, with an unspecified release date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon her taking on the role of Catherine Weaver in <i>Terminator...</i> and on the encouragement of series' composer Bear McCreary, Manson was asked by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Show_runner" title="Show runner">show runner</a> <a href="/wiki/Josh_Friedman" title="Josh Friedman">Josh Friedman</a> to perform and co-create a gospel arrangement of "Samson and Delilah" for the opening episode of the second season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSCCSaD_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-TSCCSaD-107">[107]</a></sup> After much interest, the track was released on <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator:_The_Sarah_Connor_Chronicles_(soundtrack)" title="Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles (soundtrack)">Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dungeons_and_Dragons_(Terminator:_The_Sarah_Connor_Chronicles)" title="Dungeons and Dragons (Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles)">season one</a> soundtrack at the end of 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TSCCPR_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-TSCCPR-90">[90]</a></sup> Three years later Manson recorded vocals to a track composed by <a href="/wiki/Serj_Tankian" title="Serj Tankian">Serj Tankian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steven_Sater" title="Steven Sater">Steven Sater</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The track, "The Hunger", which Sater describes as exploring "the hunger of the heart", features on their rock musical adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Prometheus_Bound" title="Prometheus Bound">Prometheus Bound</a></i>, and was recreated with fresh instrumentation and new lyrics for the digital release, exclusively through <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> worldwide. All proceeds made from sales of the single will benefit <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson has also given two tracks to <a href="/wiki/Sky_Ferreira" title="Sky Ferreira">Sky Ferreira</a>; the 2012 single "<a href="/wiki/Red_Lips" title="Red Lips">Red Lips</a>" and "I'm on Top" in 2013.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sampling">Sampling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sampling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2002, electronic group West London Deep <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sample_(music)" title="Sample (music)">sampled</a> Manson's vocal from "<a href="/wiki/You_Look_So_Fine" title="You Look So Fine">You Look So Fine</a>" in their <a href="/wiki/White_label" title="White label">white label</a> track "You're Taking Me Over". Manson refused <a href="/wiki/Authorization" title="Authorization">clearance</a> for the sample and the track was scrapped. By that point the track, and remixes by Inner City, Problem Kids and <a href="/wiki/Desyn_Masiello" title="Desyn Masiello">Desyn Masiello</a> &amp; Leon Roberts had already been circulated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The song was reworked and re-released the following year as "Gonna Make You My Lover", without Manson's vocal.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2008, Manson became engaged to record producer and Garbage sound engineer <a href="/wiki/Billy_Bush_(record_producer)" title="Billy Bush (record producer)">Billy Bush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> They were married at a Los Angeles court house in May 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheist" title="Atheist">atheist</a> but has long been interested in spirituality. She recalls, "when I was very small, I was very besotted with the church, absolutely, I loved the theatre of it and I got very involved in all the stories we were taught." Her father was also her Sunday school teacher. When she was about 12, she had an argument with her father at the dinner table, screaming at him that "religion's a sham, ... and I'm not going to church any more, it's just bullshit". She stopped going to church, but continued to have theological debates with her father every Sunday. She became disenchanted with organised religion and although she maintained an interest in spirituality she complained that she "brushed up against too many examples of 'hypocritical' spiritualists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>On aging and the pressures of women resorting to plastic surgery, Manson has said that she doesn't feel frightened, stating that she feels "very opposed to plastic surgery and cheating myself in that regard too."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changing_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-changing-15">[15]</a></sup> "I've never tried surgery or Botox and I'd like to be able to stay unobsessed by that kind of stuff", adding that "it's hard for any woman, particularly in a city where there's even a remote sense of body and beauty consciousness, and this town definitely has that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shirleydailymailtsccarticle_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-shirleydailymailtsccarticle-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson has commented on the subject of children, stating that she</p>
<blockquote>
<p>just missed that whole baby calling. I feel a lot of women think you're a freak if you feel like that, and maybe I am strange, but I never got that feeling. In some ways I wish I had had that urge, because I adore children... I feel I can live quite happily with my decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shirleydailymailtsccarticle_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-shirleydailymailtsccarticle-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Manson identifies as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feminist" title="Feminist">feminist</a> and has been hailed as a feminist icon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_work">Other work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting">Acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Manson was cast in <i><a href="/wiki/Terminator:_The_Sarah_Connor_Chronicles" title="Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles">Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles</a></i> in May 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> after being asked to appear by series creator <a href="/wiki/Josh_Friedman" title="Josh Friedman">Josh Friedman</a> and enduring a multiple audition process, beating out other actresses including <a href="/wiki/Julie_Ann_Emery" title="Julie Ann Emery">Julie Ann Emery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> She debuted in the season two premiere episode "<a href="/wiki/List_of_Terminator:_The_Sarah_Connor_Chronicles_episodes#Season_2:_2008_-_2009" title="List of Terminator: The Sarah Connor Chronicles episodes">Samson and Delilah</a>" as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_Weaver" title="Catherine Weaver">Catherine Weaver</a>, a CEO of a technology company, ZeiraCorp. At the conclusion of the episode, Weaver is revealed to be a <a href="/wiki/Shapeshifting#In_popular_culture" title="Shapeshifting">liquid-metal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-1001" title="T-1001">T-1001</a> <a href="/wiki/Terminator_(character_concept)" title="Terminator (character concept)">Terminator</a>. Manson also performed and <a href="/wiki/Arrangement" title="Arrangement">co-arranged</a> a rock and blues version of the gospel song "<a href="/wiki/Samson_and_Delilah_(song)" title="Samson and Delilah (song)">Samson and Delilah</a>" for the episode's <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">score</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Manson cites actress <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Close" title="Glenn Close">Glenn Close</a> and former British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> as her acting influences for the ambiguous character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Manson also played the human Weaver in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archive_footage" title="Archive footage">archive footage</a> viewed by the T-1001 in the episode "The Tower is Tall, But the Fall is Short".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-humanweaver_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-humanweaver-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, Manson made her first venture into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Videogame_industry" title="Videogame industry">videogame industry</a> by becoming digitally mapped to create an <a href="/wiki/Avatar_(computing)" title="Avatar (computing)">avatar</a> of herself for the <i>Guitar Hero</i> franchise. In the fifth game in the series, Manson is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unlockable_character" title="Unlockable character">unlockable character</a>, while the game also features a licensed Garbage track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuitarHero_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuitarHero-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next year, Manson was one of the final guests to appear on the cult US children's show <i><a href="/wiki/Pancake_Mountain" title="Pancake Mountain">Pancake Mountain</a></i>. Featured in a segment titled "Around the World with Shirley Manson",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Around_the_World_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Around_the_World-125">[125]</a></sup> she talked about music from other countries. She filmed five such segments but none aired before creator <a href="/wiki/Scott_Stuckey" title="Scott Stuckey">Scott Stuckey</a> and producer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JJ_Abrams" title="JJ Abrams">JJ Abrams</a> canceled the show. One segment, featuring Germany, was eventually released and featured an original theme song sung by Manson and written by Stuckey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ArondtheworldVideo_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-ArondtheworldVideo-126">[126]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_work">Charity work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shirley_Manson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Charity work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Manson has used her and Garbage's profile to raise awareness and funds for a number of causes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stars_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-stars-131">[131]</a></sup> She commissioned a Garbage branded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lipgloss" title="Lipgloss">lipgloss</a> online, with all proceeds from the sales split between <a href="/wiki/NHS_Grampian" title="NHS Grampian">Grampian Children's Cancer Research</a> and cancer treatment institutions at <a href="/wiki/Royal_Aberdeen_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Royal Aberdeen Children's Hospital">Royal Aberdeen Children's Hospital</a> in Scotland and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_Sloan_Kettering_Hospital" title="Memorial Sloan Kettering Hospital">Memorial Sloan Kettering Hospital</a> in New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-notofu_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-notofu-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="604" data-file-width="453" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg/220px-ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg/330px-ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg/440px-ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ShirleyMansonApril10-2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shirley Manson donates £51,000 to Waverley Care on behalf of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Make-up_Art_Cosmetics" title="Make-up Art Cosmetics">M•A•C AIDS Fund</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001, Manson became an ambassador for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Make-up_Art_Cosmetics" title="Make-up Art Cosmetics">M•A•C AIDS Fund</a>, fronting their fourth two-year charity lipstick <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marketing_campaign" title="Marketing campaign">marketing campaign</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, beginning with the launch of the VIVAMAC IV lipstick in March 2002, in which all proceeds of the sale of the lipstick goes to help fund AIDS charities and initiatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VMIV_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-VMIV-133">[133]</a></sup> While touring, Manson visited several AIDS charities in Amsterdam, Edinburgh, Toronto, New York, San Francisco and Madison to make several donations totalling over $300,000 on behalf of the M•A•C AIDS Fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fashioncare_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-fashioncare-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003, the M•A•C AIDS Fund linked with the <a href="/wiki/Elton_John_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elton John AIDS Foundation">Elton John AIDS Foundation</a> to produce the White Bedroom campaign,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VMIV_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-VMIV-133">[133]</a></sup> where both Elton John and Manson recorded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Service_Announcement" title="Public Service Announcement">PSAs</a> promoting <a href="/wiki/Safe_sex" title="Safe sex">condom use</a> and stating facts on AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitebedroom_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-whitebedroom-135">[135]</a></sup> By 2007, the combined six VIVAMAC campaigns had raised over $100 million U.S. dollars,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and as a former ambassador Manson accepted a cheque for £51,000 on behalf of HIV charity Waverley Care from the M•A•C AIDS Fund on 10 April 2008 at <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Nichols" title="Harvey Nichols">Harvey Nichols</a> Edinburgh store.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-impasse_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-impasse-137">[137]</a></sup> Manson had become a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patron" title="Patron">patron</a> of Waverley Care in October 2002<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> and previously hosted a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fund_raiser" title="Fund raiser">fund raiser</a> <a href="/wiki/Auction" title="Auction">auction</a> to raise funds for the charity in January 2004 which raised £45,000. A <a href="/wiki/Fender_Musical_Instruments_Corporation" title="Fender Musical Instruments Corporation">Fender</a> guitar owned by Manson raised £1,050, while other items auctioned included contributions sourced by Manson herself, from Elton John and <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stars_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-stars-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manson is also a keen lover of animals. In 2007, Manson fronted an international poster campaign for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PETA" title="PETA">PETA Europe</a>, holding the carcass of a fox under the headline "Here's the rest of your fur coat".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PETA_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-PETA-139">[139]</a></sup> Manson has also adopted a <a href="/wiki/Rescue_dog" title="Rescue dog">rescue dog</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed-breed_dog" title="Mixed-breed dog">terrier-mix</a> named <span id="veela"></span> Veela,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-notofu_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-notofu-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shirleydailymailtsccarticle_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-shirleydailymailtsccarticle-115">[115]</a></sup> named after the <a href="/wiki/Magical_creatures_in_Harry_Potter#veela" title="Magical creatures in Harry Potter">veelas</a> from the <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Potter</a></i> books.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harrypotter_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-harrypotter-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, Manson became involved with The <a href="/wiki/Pablove_Foundation" title="Pablove Foundation">Pablove Foundation</a>, a charity founded by <a href="/wiki/Dangerbird_Records" title="Dangerbird Records">Dangerbird Records</a> head <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Castelaz" title="Jeff Castelaz">Jeff Castelaz</a>, whose son Pablo succumbed to cancer the following year. Castelaz, whose family Manson had befriended in the 90s, had asked Manson to sing "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars%3F" title="Life on Mars?">Life on Mars?</a>" at their sons' memorial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Funds raised for The Pablove Foundation fund pediatric cancer research and educational and quality of life programming for families dealing with childhood cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShirlYT_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-ShirlYT-142">[142]</a></sup> Manson reformed Garbage to contribute an exclusive track, "Witness to Your Love", to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charity_album" title="Charity album">charity album</a> for the Foundation;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GLH_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-GLH-143">[143]</a></sup> signed off a Pablove poster for auction on <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShirlYT_142-1"><a href="#cite_note-ShirlYT-142">[142]</a></sup> Manson also hosted a fundraiser headlined by the <a href="/wiki/Silversun_Pickups" title="Silversun Pickups">Silversun Pickups</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SSPUfundraiser_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-SSPUfundraiser-144">[144]</a></sup> and performed acoustically on-stage at a second fundraiser with Butch Vig and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tom_Gabel" title="Tom Gabel">Tom Gabel</a> (for a rendition of "Witness...") and with Greg Kurstin (for a cover of Pablo's favourite song, <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>'s "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_on_Mars%3F" title="Life on Mars?">Life on Mars?</a>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pablovefundraiser_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pablovefundraiser-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Shirley Manson donated two hand-decorated T-shirts to Binki Shapiro's (of the band <a href="/wiki/Little_Joy" title="Little Joy">Little Joy</a>) online charity auction "Crafts for a Cause" to raise money for victims of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>. The two T-shirts raised a total of $1522.00, which was donated to the <a href="/wiki/Artists_for_Peace_and_Justice" title="Artists for Peace and Justice">Artists for Peace and Justice</a> organisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015, Manson headlined Pablove 6, the sixth-annual fundraiser for the Pablove Foundation. She made a special appearance with Chicago-based David Bowie tribute band <a href="/wiki/Sons_of_the_Silent_Age" title="Sons of the Silent Age">Sons of the Silent Age</a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Matt_Walker_(drummer)" title="Matt Walker (drummer)">Matt Walker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Connelly_(musician)" title="Chris Connelly (musician)">Chris Connelly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Json_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Json-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
